I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -1.15357*x - 1.15357*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.42262*sin(t)**

Let me analyze the GT structure:
- A linear term in x: `-1.15357*x`
- A term `x*exp(-|x|)`: `-1.15357*x*exp(-|x|)`
- A sinusoidal term in t: `0.42262*sin(t)`

Key observations about `x*exp(-|x|)`:
- This is an odd function of x
- It cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, rational functions, or simple combinations thereof
- `exp(-|x|)` is NOT the same as `exp(-x)` or `exp(x)` since |x| matters for negative x

Let me check each candidate systematically.

**Candidate 1:** Contains terms with `1/(c1*|x|+1)`, `x*|x|/(c1*|x|+1)`, `x*|x|^c9`, and `cos(c4*t+c5)`. The rational terms in |x| and polynomial/power terms cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` exactly. The `cos` can match `sin` with phase shift. But the x-dependent part cannot match.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Rational functions of x (polynomials divided by `c1+x²`) plus `cos`. These are rational functions of x, which cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x/(c1*x²+1) + c2*exp(c3*x) + c4*exp(c5*x) + c6*x + c7*cos(c8*t+c9)`

The GT has `x*exp(-|x|)`. Note that `exp(-|x|)` can be written as:
- For x > 0: exp(-x)
- For x < 0: exp(x)

So `x*exp(-|x|)` equals:
- For x > 0: x*exp(-x)
- For x < 0: x*exp(x)

Can `c2*exp(c3*x) + c4*exp(c5*x)` match `-1.15357*x*exp(-|x|)`? No, because exp functions are not equal to x*exp(-|x|). The candidate has pure exponentials, not x times exponentials. Also `c0*x/(c1*x²+1)` is a rational function. The sum of exponentials and rational functions cannot equal x*exp(-|x|).
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** Same structure as Candidate 3 but with sin instead of cos. Same analysis applies.
